# pypge Codebase Architecture Summary

## 1. Directory Structure

```
/Users/tony/verdverm/pge-jax/pypge/
├── pypge/                          # Core library package
│   ├── __init__.py                 # Empty namespace
│   ├── base.py                     # DEAP-derived: Toolbox, Fitness base classes
│   ├── creator.py                  # DEAP-derived: Dynamic class creation (FitnessCalculator)
│   ├── model.py                    # Model class: wraps sympy expressions
│   ├── expand.py                   # Grower class: expression tree enumeration
│   ├── search.py                   # PGE class: main search loop (prioritized expansion)
│   ├── selection.py                # NSGA-II, SPEA-II, log-non-dominated sorting
│   ├── evaluate.py                 # Fit, Eval, Score functions (lmfit + sklearn)
│   ├── fitness_funcs.py            # Multi-objective fitness construction
│   ├── filters.py                  # Expression validity filters
│   ├── algebra.py                  # Symbolic algebraic manipulations (expand/factor/simplify)
│   ├── memoize.py                  # Memoizer + Mapper: expression deduplication
│   ├── parallel.py                 # Multiprocessing workers for eval, algebra, expand
│   └── timer.py                    # Timing utilities
│   ├── benchmarks/                 # Benchmark problem generators
│   │   ├── __init__.py             # Empty
│   │   ├── explicit.py             # Koza, Lipson, Nguyen, Korns benchmarks
│   │   ├── chaotic_pendulum.py     # Chaotic pendulum problem
│   │   ├── yeast.py                # Yeast gene regulation data
│   │   └── diffeq.py               # Differential equation problems
├── experiments/                    # Experiment runner
│   ├── main.py                     # CLI entry point for running PGE
│   └── 01_baseline/                # Baseline experiment configs
├── data/                           # Training data
│   └── datagen/                    # Data generation scripts
├── test/                           # Unit tests
│   ├── test_odeint.py
│   ├── test_lmfit.py
│   └── test_sample.py
├── notebooks/                      # Jupyter notebooks
├── dockers/                        # Docker configurations
├── setup.py, setup.cfg             # Package setup
├── requirements.txt                # Dependencies
├── README.md                       # Documentation
└── Dockerfile, dockerize.sh        # Containerization
```

## 2. Core Data Structures

### Model (`pypge/model.py`)

The `Model` class is the central data structure. Every candidate expression is wrapped in a `Model`:

```python
class Model:
    # Identification
    id: int           # Unique model ID
    iter_id: int      # Which iteration it was created in
    parent_id: int    # Parent model ID (for tree tracking)
    gen_relation: str # How this model was generated ("first_gen", "var_xpnd", "add_xpnd", "mul_xpnd", "shrunk", etc.)

    # State flags (boolean lifecycle)
    inited, memoized, algebrad, peeked, peek_queued, peek_popped
    evaluated, queued, popped, expanded, finalized, errored

    # Expression
    orig: sympy.Expr  # Original expression before coefficient rewriting
    expr: sympy.Expr  # Expanded expression after rewrite_coeff()
    pretty: str       # Cached pretty-printed string

    # Variables and coefficients
    xs: list          # Input variable symbols
    cs: list          # Coefficient symbols (C_0, C_1, ...)
    params: lmfit.Parameters  # Optimized coefficient values

    # Pre-computed symbolic Jacobian
    jac: list         # [sympy.diff(expr, c) for c in cs]

    # Initial coefficient guess
    guess: list       # [1.0, 1.0, ...]

    # Size metrics
    sz: int           # Tree size
    psz: int          # Penalized tree size (functions get +2 penalty)
    jsz: int          # Jacobian size
    jpsz: int         # Penalized Jacobian size
    ncs: int          # Number of coefficients

    # Peek (fast, partial) fitness
    peek_score, peek_r2, peek_evar, peek_aic, peek_bic, peek_redchi

    # Full (slow, complete) fitness
    score, r2, evar, aic, bic, redchi, mae, mse, rmae, rmse, adj_r2, chisqr

    # Improvement over parent
    improve_score, improve_r2, improve_evar, improve_aic, improve_bic, improve_redchi

    # Fit result from lmfit
    fit_result: lmfit.MinimizerResult
```

Key method: `rewrite_coeff()` converts bare `sympy.Symbol('C')` leaves into `C_0, C_1, C_2, ...` and creates `lmfit.Parameters` for optimization.

### Fitness (`pypge/base.py`, `pypge/creator.py`)

Adapted from DEAP:

- **`Fitness`** (base.py): Abstract base with `weights` (tuple), `values` property, `dominates()`, and lexicographic comparison operators. Negative weights = minimization, positive = maximization.
- **`FitnessCalculator`** (dynamically created by `fitness_funcs.py`): A concrete `Fitness` subclass with weights determined by the fitness function parameters.
- **`Toolbox`** (base.py): Registry for evolutionary operators (clone, map, and custom-registered functions).

### Population / Heap Lists

The PGE class maintains several lists of `Model` objects:

- **`self.models`**: All models ever created (indexed by `id`)
- **`self.hmap`**: Dict mapping `expr -> Model` for deduplication
- **`self.final`**: All fully evaluated, finalized models
- **`self.nsga2_list`**: Models waiting to be expanded (the "population")
- **`self.nsga2_peek`**: Models that have been peek-evaluated, waiting for full evaluation
- **`self.multi_expanders[i]['nsga2_list']`**: Per-expander population heaps
- **`self.multi_expanders[i]['grower']`**: Per-expander `Grower` instance

## 3. Module-by-Module Breakdown

### 3.1 `model.py` -- Model Class

**Purpose**: Wraps a SymPy expression and manages its lifecycle state, coefficient parameters, and symbolic Jacobian.

**Key functions**:
- `__init__(expr, xs, cs, p_id, reln)`: Initializes model, calls `rewrite_coeff()`, pre-computes symbolic Jacobian `jac`, creates `lmfit.Parameters`
- `rewrite_coeff()`: Replaces bare `C` symbols with `C_0, C_1, ...`, creates parameters dict
- `_rewrite_coeff_helper(expr, ii)`: Recursive helper that walks the expression tree and replaces `C` atoms
- `size()`, `calc_tree_size()`, `calc_jac_size()`: Compute tree size with function penalty (+2 per function node)
- `pretty_expr()`: Substitute coefficient values and return string representation

### 3.2 `expand.py` -- Expression Expansion (Grower)

**Purpose**: Implements the core grammar-based expression enumeration. Takes existing models and produces expanded children.

**Key class: `Grower`**

Configuration parameters (all configurable via kwargs):
- `func_level`: "linear" or "nonlin" -- whether functions use affine transforms `f(C*x+C)` (nonlinear) or just `f(x)` (linear)
- `init_level`: "low", "med", "high" -- complexity of first-generation models
- `grow_level` / `subs_level` / `adds_level` / `muls_level`: "low", "med", "high" -- expansion complexity levels
- `add_xtop`: Whether to extend at the top level of additions
- `shrinker`: Whether to try removing terms from additions
- `grow_filter`: Whether to avoid duplicate terms in additions
- `limiting_depth`: Depth limit for variable substitution

**Pre-computed expression pools** (built in `__init__`):
- `xs_pow1` through `xs_pow4`: Powers of input variables (x, 1/x, x^2, 1/x^2, etc.)
- `wout_c_xsN_muls`: Variable products without coefficients
- `with_c_xsN_muls`: Variable products with coefficient `C * ...`
- `wout_c_linear_funcs`: `f(variable_product)` for each function
- `wout_c_nonlin_funcs`: `f(C * variable_product + C)` for each function
- `with_c_func_exprs` / `wout_c_func_exprs`: Full function expressions with/without coefficients
- `var_sub_terms`, `add_extend_terms`, `mul_extend_terms`: Expansion term pools at varying complexity

**Key methods**:
- `first_exprs()`: Generate initial generation models from scratch. Creates combinations of variable products and function expressions, adds `+C` variants, uniquifies, and wraps in `Model` objects with `gen_relation="first_gen"`
- `grow(M)`: Expand a single model. Returns children from 5 expansion types:
  1. **`_var_sub()`**: Variable substitution -- replaces input variable occurrences with more complex expressions (recursive)
  2. **`_add_extend()`**: Addition extension -- adds terms to `Add` nodes (recursive)
  3. **`_mul_extend()`**: Multiplication extension -- adds factors to `Mul` nodes (recursive)
  4. **`_add_extend_top_level()`**: Top-level addition extension (non-recursive, with more complex multiplication)
  5. **`_shrinker()`**: Term removal from `Add` nodes (recursive)
- `_var_sub(expr, limit_sub, depth)`: Recursively substitutes input variables with pre-computed term pools. Respects depth limits and function context (limits substitution inside non-Add/Mul nodes)
- `_toggle_plus_C(expr)`: Adds or removes a bare `C` from an addition
- `_uniquify(exprs)`: Removes duplicates via `expr.evalf()` hashing

**Note**: There is a typo in `map_names_to_funcs()` -- it references `func` instead of `funcs` on line 28, suggesting a bug.

### 3.3 `search.py` -- PGE Search Loop

**Purpose**: The main Prioritized Grammar Enumeration algorithm. Orchestrates expansion, filtering, memoization, algebraic manipulation, evaluation, and selection.

**Key class: `PGE`**

**Configuration** (all overrideable via kwargs):
- `workers`: Number of multiprocessing workers (0 = single-process)
- `queue_size`: Size of multiprocessing queues
- `max_iter`: Number of search iterations
- `pop_count`: Number of models to pop from heap per expansion
- `peek_count`: Number of models to peek-evaluate per iteration (default = 2 * pop_count)
- `peek_npts`: Number of data points for peek evaluation (0 = skip peek, use full data)
- `min_size`/`max_size`, `min_depth`/`max_depth`: Size/depth bounds
- `max_power`: Maximum power exponent allowed
- `algebra_methods`: ["expand", "factor"] -- symbolic simplification methods
- `err_method`: Error metric name ("mse", "rmse", "r2", etc.)
- `fitness_func_params`: List like `["normalize", "-(1)jpsz", "-score", "+bic", ...]`
- `multi_expander_params`: List of per-expander configs (each with `pop_count`, `usable_funcs`, `grow_params`)

**Data setup**:
- `set_data(X_train, Y_train)`: Sets training data, samples `peek_npts` random points for peek evaluation
- If `remote_eval=True`, sends data to remote evaluation server via WebSocket

**Main API** (sklearn-compatible):
```python
pge = PGE(**config)
pge.fit(X_train, Y_train)  # Triggers preloop() -> loop(max_iter) -> finalize()
```

#### Preloop (Initialization)

1. Generate first expressions via `multi_expanders[0]['grower'].first_exprs()`
2. Filter models: `filter_models()` -- removes invalid expressions
3. Memoize: `memoize_models()` -- deduplication via expression hash
4. Algebraic manipulation: `algebra_models()` -- apply expand/factor
5. Filter and memoize algebraic results
6. Peek-evaluate or full-evaluate the initial batch
7. Push to `nsga2_peek` heap and `nsga2_list` population heap
8. Print best models

#### Main Loop (per iteration)

For each of `N` iterations:

1. **Multi-expand and grow**: For each expander:
   - Pop `pop_count` models from the expander's `nsga2_list` using NSGA-II selection
   - Expand each popped model via `grower.grow()`
   - Push remaining models back to the heap
   - Collect all expanded children

2. **Filter**: Remove invalid models via `filter_models()`

3. **Memoize**: Deduplicate via expression hash

4. **Algebraic manipulation**: Apply expand/factor to unique models

5. **Filter and memoize** algebraic results again

6. **Progressive evaluation**:
   - Peek-evaluate unique models on `peek_npts` data points
   - Push peek'd models to `nsga2_peek` heap
   - Pop best models from peek heap for full evaluation

7. **Full evaluation**: Fit and score models on full training data

8. **Final push**: Add fully evaluated models to `self.final`

9. **Population push**: Add evaluated models back to the expansion population heap

#### Key Methods

- `filter_models(models)`: Applies `filters.default_filters` to each model
- `memoize_models(models)`: Deduplicates via `self.hmap[expr]` lookup; returns only new unique models
- `expand_models(models, grower)`: Calls `grow_models()` (single-process) or `expand_models_multiprocess()` (multi-process)
- `algebra_models(models)`: Applies each algebra method to each model
- `peek_push_models(models)`: Adds peek-evaluated models to `nsga2_peek`
- `peek_pop()`: Pops best models from peek heap for full evaluation
- `final_push(models)`: Adds fully evaluated models to `self.final`
- `heap_push(heap_list, models)`: Extends a heap list with valid models
- `heap_pop(heap_list, pop_count, fitness_calc)`: Selects models via NSGA-II or log-non-dominated sort
- `eval_models(models, peek)`: Dispatches to local or remote evaluation
- `eval_models_local()`: Single-process evaluation loop
- `eval_models_multiprocess()`: Multiprocessing via `eval_in_queue`/`eval_out_queue`
- `eval_models_remote()`: WebSocket-based remote evaluation
- `print_best(count)`: Prints top models from `self.final`
- `finalize()`: Generates final Pareto fronts, stops workers, closes connections
- `get_final_paretos()`: Returns final Pareto front list

### 3.4 `selection.py` -- Multi-Objective Selection

**Purpose**: Implements non-dominated sorting and selection operators for multi-objective optimization. Taken from DEAP.

**Key functions**:

- **`selNSGA2(individuals, k, nd='standard')`**: NSGA-II selection operator. Sorts into Pareto fronts, assigns crowding distances, fills selection from best fronts, breaking ties by crowding distance.
  - `nd='standard'`: Uses `sortNondominated()` (O(M*N^2))
  - `nd='log'`: Uses `sortLogNondominated()` (reduced runtime complexity)

- **`sortNondominated(individuals, k)`**: Standard fast non-dominated sorting. O(M*N^2) time complexity.

- **`sortLogNondominated(individuals, k)`**: Generalized Reduced Run-Time Complexity Non-Dominated Sorting (Fortin et al. 2013). Uses recursive divide-and-conquer with sweep procedures (`sweepA`, `sweepB`) for O(N log^(M-1) N) complexity. This is the **primary sorting method used by PGE** (`use_nsga2=True`).

- **`assignCrowdingDist(individuals)`**: Assigns crowding distance to each individual for diversity maintenance.

- **`selSPEA2(individuals, k)`**: Strength Pareto EA II selection. Computes strength fitnesses, density estimates, and selects.

- **`selTournamentDCD(individuals, k)`**: Tournament selection based on dominance and crowding distance.

- **`isDominated(wvalues1, wvalues2)`**: Checks if wvalues1 is dominated by wvalues2.

- **`sortNDHelperA`, `sortNDHelperB`**: Recursive helpers for log non-dominated sorting.
- **`splitA`, `splitB`**: Median-based partitioning for divide-and-conquer.
- **`sweepA`, `sweepB`**: Geometric sweep procedures for 2D dominance testing.

### 3.5 `evaluate.py` -- Model Evaluation

**Purpose**: Fits model coefficients and computes error metrics.

**Key functions**:

- **`Fit(modl, xs, X_train, Y_train, MAXFEV=100)`**: Uses `lmfit.minimize()` with Levenberg-Marquardt (`Dfun=dfunc, col_deriv=1`). The objective function computes residuals `y_pred - y_train`. The Jacobian function `dfunc` computes per-coefficient Jacobian columns, using pre-computed symbolic Jacobians from `modl.jac`.

- **`Eval(modl, xs, X_input)`**: Substitutes coefficient values into the expression, then `sympy.lambdify(xs, eqn, "numpy")` to create a callable. Returns predictions.

- **`EvalJac(modl, jac_eqn, xs, X_input)`**: Evaluates a pre-computed symbolic Jacobian expression.

- **`Score(y_true, y_pred, err_metric)`**: Computes error metrics via sklearn: r2, evar, mae, mse, rmae, rmse.

- **`eval_model(modl, vars, X_train, Y_train, err_method, MAXFEV=100)`**: Full evaluation pipeline:
  1. Call `Fit()` to optimize coefficients
  2. Call `Eval()` to get predictions
  3. Compute `score`, `r2`, `evar` via `Score()`
  4. Extract `aic`, `bic`, `chisqr`, `redchi` from `fit_result`
  5. Returns `True` if successful, `False` if errored

### 3.6 `fitness_funcs.py` -- Multi-Objective Fitness Construction

**Purpose**: Dynamically constructs the fitness evaluation function from configuration parameters.

**Key functions**:

- **`build_fitness_calc(params)`**: Main entry point. `params` is a list like `["normalize", "-(1)jpsz", "-score", "+bic"]`.
  - If "normalize" is present, normalizes each objective across the population by L2 norm
  - Builds a `FitnessCalculator` class and a value extractor
  - Returns either `fitness_calc_norm` or `fitness_calc_raw`

- **`build_fitness_weights(params)`**: Parses fitness params to extract weights:
  - `"-(1)jpsz"` -> weight = -1.0 (minimize jpsz)
  - `"+bic"` -> weight = +1.0 (maximize bic)
  - `"score"` -> weight = -1.0 (implicit minimization)

- **`build_value_extractor(params)`**: Creates a function that extracts the specified attributes from each model.

- **`fitness_calc_raw(extractor)`**: Sets fitness values independently per model.

- **`fitness_calc_norm(extractor)`**: Normalizes each objective column across all models by L2 norm before setting fitness values.

### 3.7 `filters.py` -- Expression Filters

**Purpose**: Validates candidate expressions, removing invalid or degenerate ones.

**Default filters** (`default_filters`):
- `filter_too_big`: Removes models with `size() > 64`
- `filter_has_int_coeff`: Removes expressions with hardcoded integer coefficients (not using `C` symbols)
- `filter_has_big_pow`: Removes expressions with power exponents > 6
- `filter_just_C`: Removes expressions that are just the coefficient symbol `C`
- `filter_no_C`: Removes expressions with no coefficients (constant expressions)
- `filter_has_coeff_pow`: Removes expressions like `C^2` (coefficient raised to a power)

**`filter_models(models, filters)`**: Applies all filters to all models. Returns models that pass all filters.

**`filter_model(modl, expr, filters)`**: Walks the expression tree via `preorder_traversal` and checks each node against all filters.

### 3.8 `algebra.py` -- Symbolic Algebraic Manipulation

**Purpose**: Applies symbolic simplification to expressions.

**Key functions**:

- **`manip_model(modl, method)`**: Applies a simplification method to a model. Returns a new `Model` if the expression changed, or `(None, "same")` if unchanged.
- **`do_simp(expr, method)`**: Applies the specified method:
  - `"simplify"`: `sympy.simplify(expr)`
  - `"expand"`: `sympy.expand(expr)`
  - `"factor"`: `sympy.factor(expr)`

### 3.9 `memoize.py` -- Expression Deduplication

**Purpose**: Prevents duplicate expressions from being evaluated.

**Key classes**:

- **`Memoizer`**: Indexes models by expression hash.
  - `insert(model)`: Inserts a model into the index. Returns `True` if new, `False` if duplicate.
  - `lookup(model)`: Returns `(found, model)` tuple.
  - `encode(expr)`: Serializes an expression tree into a list of integer codes for remote evaluation.

- **`Mapper`**: Maps SymPy node types to integer codes for serialization.
  - `Mul` -> 8, `Add` -> 9, `Pow` -> 10, `Abs` -> 12, `sqrt` -> 13, `log` -> 14, `exp` -> 15, `cos` -> 16, `sin` -> 17, `tan` -> 18
  - `Symbol` (variable) -> 5, `Symbol` (coefficient) -> 1, integers -> 2

### 3.10 `parallel.py` -- Multiprocessing Workers

**Purpose**: Worker processes for parallel evaluation, algebra, and expansion.

**Key functions** (each runs as a separate process):

- **`unwrap_self_peek_model_queue(PGE)`**: Peek evaluation worker. Reads from `peek_in_queue`, calls `evaluate.eval_model()` on peek data, writes results to `peek_out_queue`.
- **`unwrap_self_eval_model_queue(PGE)`**: Full evaluation worker. Reads from `eval_in_queue`, calls `evaluate.eval_model()` on full training data, writes to `eval_out_queue`.
- **`unwrap_self_alge_model_queue(PGE)`**: Algebra worker. Reads `(index, model, method)` from `alge_in_queue`, calls `algebra.manip_model()`, writes to `alge_out_queue`.
- **`unwrap_self_expd_model_queue(PGE)`**: Expansion worker. Reads `(index, model, grower)` from `expd_in_queue`, calls `grower.grow()`, writes to `expd_out_queue`.

All workers use a sentinel `None` value to signal shutdown.

### 3.11 `base.py` and `creator.py` -- DEAP Foundations

These are adapted from the DEAP library:

- **`base.Toolbox`**: Registry for evolutionary operators. Supports `register(alias, function, *args, **kwargs)` with automatic `functools.partial` binding.
- **`base.Fitness`**: Abstract fitness class with weighted multi-objective comparison, lexicographic operators, and dominance checking.
- **`creator.create(name, base, **kargs)`**: Dynamically creates new classes. Used to create `FitnessCalculator` at runtime with specific weights.

### 3.12 `timer.py` -- Timing Utilities

**`timewith`**: Context manager for timing. Supports checkpoints and finalization with elapsed time reporting.

## 4. The Main Search/Evolution Loop

```
                    ┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
                    │              PGE.fit(X, Y)                   │
                    │  ┌───────────────────────────────────────┐  │
                    │  │           PRELOOP                      │  │
                    │  │ 1. Generate first_exprs()              │  │
                    │  │ 2. Filter (remove invalid)             │  │
                    │  │ 3. Memoize (deduplicate)               │  │
                    │  │ 4. Algebra (expand/factor)             │  │
                    │  │ 5. Filter + Memoize again              │  │
                    │  │ 6. Peek-evaluate OR full-evaluate      │  │
                    │  │ 7. Push to nsga2_list (population)     │  │
                    │  │ 8. Push to final (fully evaluated)     │  │
                    │  └───────────────────────────────────────┘  │
                    │                                              │
                    │  ┌───────────────────────────────────────┐  │
                    │  │           MAIN LOOP (N iterations)     │  │
                    │  │                                       │  │
                    │  │  For each expander:                   │  │
                    │  │    1. heap_pop() -- NSGA-II select    │  │
                    │  │    2. grower.grow() -- expand models  │  │
                    │  │                                       │  │
                    │  │ 3. Filter expanded models             │  │
                    │  │ 4. Memoize (deduplicate)              │  │
                    │  │ 5. Algebra (expand/factor)            │  │
                    │  │ 6. Filter + Memoize again             │  │
                    │  │                                       │  │
                    │  │ 7. Peek-evaluate unique models        │  │
                    │  │ 8. Push to nsga2_peek heap            │  │
                    │  │ 9. heap_pop(nsga2_peek)               │  │
                    │  │ 10. Full-evaluate selected models     │  │
                    │  │ 11. Push to final                     │  │
                    │  │ 12. Push to nsga2_list                │  │
                    │  └───────────────────────────────────────┘  │
                    │                                              │
                    │  ┌───────────────────────────────────────┐  │
                    │  │          FINALIZE                      │  │
                    │  │ 1. Combine final + nsga2_list         │  │
                    │  │ 2. sortLogNondominated()              │  │
                    │  │ 3. Print Pareto fronts                │  │
                    │  │ 4. Stop workers                       │  │
                    │  └───────────────────────────────────────┘  │
                    └─────────────────────────────────────────────┘
```

## 5. How Components Connect

```
                    User / Experiment Runner
                           │
                    experiments/main.py
                           │
                    PGE(**config).fit(X, Y)
                           │
                    ┌──────┴─────────────────────────────────┐
                    │                                         │
              expand.py                              evaluate.py
              Grower.grow()                         Fit() + lmfit
              (expression creation)                (coefficient optimization)
                    │                                         │
                    ▼                                         ▼
              filters.py                            fitness_funcs.py
              (remove invalid expressions)        (multi-objective scoring)
                    │                                         │
                    ▼                                         ▼
              memoize.py                            selection.py
              (deduplicate)                         (NSGA-II / log-ND sort)
                    │                                         │
                    ▼                                         ▼
              algebra.py                            parallel.py
              (expand/factor)                       (multiprocessing)
```

**Data flow for each model**:
1. **Creation**: `Grower.first_exprs()` or `Grower.grow()` produces a `sympy.Expr`
2. **Model wrapping**: `Model(expr)` -- calls `rewrite_coeff()`, computes symbolic Jacobian
3. **Filtering**: `filters.filter_models()` removes invalid expressions
4. **Deduplication**: `memoize_models()` checks `self.hmap[expr]`
5. **Algebra**: `algebra.manip_model()` applies expand/factor
6. **Deduplication again**: After algebra
7. **Peek evaluation**: `evaluate.eval_model()` on subset of data (fast)
8. **Selection**: `selection.selNSGA2()` or `selection.sortLogNondominated()` picks which peek'd models get full evaluation
9. **Full evaluation**: `evaluate.eval_model()` on full data (slow, with lmfit optimization)
10. **Fitness assignment**: `fitness_funcs.build_fitness_calc()` sets `model.fitness.values`
11. **Population update**: Models pushed to `nsga2_list` for future expansion or `final` for output

## 6. Entry Points

1. **Programmatic**: `from pypge.search import PGE; pge = PGE(**config); pge.fit(X, Y)`
2. **CLI**: `python experiments/main.py <config.yaml> <input.csv> <output_dir>`
3. **Docker**: `docker run --rm -it --name pypge -v \`pwd\`:/pycode verdverm/pypge-experiments /bin/bash` then `./run.sh`

## 7. Dependencies

- **numpy**: Array operations, random data generation
- **sympy**: Symbolic expression trees, lambdify, simplification
- **lmfit**: Levenberg-Marquardt coefficient optimization
- **sklearn**: Error metrics (r2_score, mean_squared_error, etc.)
- **networkx**: Expression relationship graph tracking
- **pandas**: Data I/O
- **websocket-client**: Remote evaluation server communication
- **pyyaml**: Configuration file parsing
</task_result>
```

## Comprehensive State of the pge-jax Port

### 1. Full Directory Structure

```
pge-jax/
├── pge_jax/                    # JAX package source (PORTED)

│   ├── model.py                # JAXModel - sympy -> JAX wrapper
│   ├── optimize.py             # LM + BFGS optimizers in JAX

│   ├── test_metrics.py         # 11 tests

│       ├── selection.py        # NSGA-II, SPEA-II selection

│       ├── pge_init_method_*.go  # Initialization strategies
│       ├── pge_bbsr.go         # Best-first beam search regression
│       └── ipre_trie.go        # I-prefix trie for deduplication
├── ffx/                        # Reference: FFX implementation
├── pysr/                       # Reference: PySymbolicRegression
├── pyproject.toml              # Build config, deps
├── README.md                   # User documentation
├── Makefile                    # clone-prior-art target
├── AGENTS.md                   # Agent instructions
└── LICENSE
```

### 2. What Has Been Ported (Fully Implemented)

#### `pge_jax/model.py` (208 lines)
- **`JAXModel`** class: wraps sympy expressions with JAX evaluation
  - `_extract_coeffs_and_vars()`: splits symbols into coefficients (`C_*`, `C[...]`) and variables
  - `_build_jax_functions()`: `sympy.lambdify(modules="jax")` wrapper with coefficient array unpacking
  - Jacobian via `jax.jacfwd` + `jax.vmap` over data points
  - `predict()`, `jacobian()`, `pretty_expr()` methods
  - Handles edge cases: constant expressions, no coefficients, no variables, multivariate

#### `pge_jax/optimize.py` (228 lines)
- **`FitResult`** dataclass: success, coefficients, predictions, cost, n_residuals, n_params, message, nfev
- **`fit_levenberg_marquardt()`**: Custom JAX-native LM optimizer
  - Damped normal equations: `(J^T J + mu I) d = -J^T r`
  - Adaptive damping with blowup protection (`mu > 1e12`)
  - Multiple convergence criteria: cost tolerance, relative change, coefficient change
- **`fit_least_squares()`**: BFGS wrapper via `jax.scipy.optimize.minimize` with optional bounds via penalty method

#### `pge_jax/metrics.py` (86 lines)
- 9 JAX-native metrics: `rmse`, `mae`, `mse`, `r2`, `explained_variance`, `aic`, `bic`, `chisqr`, `redchi`, `rmae`
- All are JAX-transformable (work with `jax.grad`, `jax.vmap`, etc.)

#### `pge_jax/evaluate.py` (138 lines)
- **`EvalResult`** dataclass: fit + all metrics (score, r2, evar, aic, bic, chisqr, redchi, mae, rmae, predictions)
- **`fit_model()`**: High-level fit with method selection (`"lm"` or `"ls"`)
- **`predict()`**: Evaluate model at given coefficients
- **`evaluate()`**: Compute all regression metrics

#### `pge_jax/__init__.py` (20 lines)
- 12 public exports: `JAXModel`, `fit_levenberg_marquardt`, `fit_least_squares`, 7 metrics, `fit_model`, `predict`, `evaluate`

### 3. Test Structure and Coverage

**4 test files, 41 tests total**, all covering the ported code:

| File | Class | Tests | Coverage |
|------|-------|-------|----------|
| `test_model.py` | `TestExtractCoeffsAndVars` (4) + `TestJAXModel` (9) | 13 | Coefficient extraction, linear/quadratic/trig models, Jacobians, multivariate, edge cases |
| `test_optimize.py` | `TestFitLevenbergMarquardt` (7) + `TestFitLeastSquares` (2) | 9 | LM with analytic/numeric Jacobian, noisy data, bounds, FitResult attributes |
| `test_metrics.py` | 10 metric tests | 10 | Perfect/noisy predictions, JAX transformability (jax.grad) |
| `test_evaluate.py` | `TestFitModel` (4) + `TestPredict` (1) + `TestEvaluate` (3) | 8 | Full pipeline: create -> fit -> evaluate, both "lm" and "ls" methods |

### 4. What Has NOT Been Ported (PGE Search Logic)

These are the core PGE components that need to be built:

#### A. **Expression Expansion** (`pypge/expand.py` - 604 lines)
The `Grower` class implements PGE's expression growth operators:
- **`first_exprs()`**: Generate initial population
- **`grow()`**: Expand a single model via 4 operators:
  - `_var_sub()`: Variable substitution (replace variables with more complex terms)
  - `_add_extend()`: Add a term to an Add expression
  - `_mul_extend()`: Widen a Mul term
  - `_shrinker()`: Remove terms from an Add expression
- **`_toggle_plus_C()`**: Add/remove free coefficient
- **Policy levels** (`low`/`med`/`high`) controlling expansion complexity
- **`_uniquify()`**: Deduplication via `evalf()`

#### B. **Search Loop** (`pypge/search.py` - 1429 lines)
The `PGE` class:
- **`fit()`**: sklearn-style entry point
- **`preloop()`**: Generate, filter, memoize, algebra, peek-evaluate, full-evaluate initial population
- **`loop()`**: Main iteration: pop from heap -> expand -> filter -> memoize -> algebra -> peek-eval -> full-eval -> push to final and selection heaps
- **`finalize()`**: Generate final Pareto fronts
- **`peek_pop()` / `peek_push()`**: Progressive evaluation heap management
- **`heap_push()` / `heap_pop()`**: NSGA-II selection from population
- **`eval_models()`**: Local or multiprocessing evaluation
- **`expand_models()`**: Grow expressions
- **`algebra_models()`**: Apply algebraic simplifications
- **`memoize_models()`**: Expression deduplication via hash map

#### C. **Multi-Objective Selection** (`pypge/selection.py` - 617 lines)
- **`selNSGA2()`**: NSGA-II fast non-dominated sorting + crowding distance
- **`sortLogNondominated()`**: Generalized reduced run-time complexity ND sort (Fortin et al. 2013)
- **`selSPEA2()`**: SPEA-II strength Pareto evolution
- **`selTournamentDCD()`**: Tournament selection by dominance + crowding distance
- Helper: `assignCrowdingDist()`, `isDominated()`, `sweepA/B()`, `splitA/B()`

#### D. **Fitness Calculation** (`pypge/fitness_funcs.py` - 103 lines)
- **`build_fitness_calc()`**: Build fitness calculator from parameter list
- Normalized vs raw fitness calculation
- Weight specification: `"-score(1.0)"`, `"+r2(0.5)"` syntax
- Value extraction from model attributes

#### E. **Expression Filters** (`pypge/filters.py` - 75 lines)
- `filter_just_C()`: Reject bare coefficient expressions
- `filter_no_C()`: Reject expressions with no coefficients
- `filter_too_big()`: Size limit (default 64)
- `filter_has_int_coeff()`: Reject expressions with hardcoded integer coefficients
- `filter_has_big_pow()`: Reject exponents > 6
- `filter_has_coeff_pow()`: Reject coefficient raised to a power

#### F. **Algebraic Manipulation** (`pypge/algebra.py` - 155 lines)
- `manip_model()`: Apply simplification to a model
- Methods: `simplify`, `expand`, `factor`
- Returns "same" if expression unchanged (no need for new node)

#### G. **Memoization / Deduplication** (`pypge/memoize.py` - 180 lines)
- `Memoizer` class: hash-based expression deduplication
- `Mapper` class: expression serialization to integer arrays (for trie-based dedup in go-pge)

#### H. **Parallel Execution** (`pypge/parallel.py` - 151 lines)
- Multiprocessing workers for: peek evaluation, full evaluation, algebra, expansion

#### I. **Original Model Class** (`pypge/model.py` - 217 lines)
- State tracking (inited, memoized, peeked, evaluated, finalized, etc.)
- `rewrite_coeff()`: Convert bare `C` to `C_0`, `C_1`, etc.
- `size()`, `calc_tree_size()`, `calc_jac_size()`: Complexity metrics
- `pretty_expr()`: String representation with fitted coefficients
- `lmfit`-based parameter management

### 5. Dependencies in `pyproject.toml`

**Core dependencies:**
- `jax>=0.4.30`, `jaxlib>=0.4.30` - Array computation + autodiff
- `numpy>=1.26` - Numeric operations
- `scipy>=1.12` - For `jax.scipy.optimize.minimize`
- `sympy>=1.13` - Symbolic expression representation
- `networkx>=3.3` - Graph storage (for relationship graph in PGE search)
- `tqdm>=4.66` - Progress bars

**Optional:**
- `dev`: pytest, pytest-cov, ruff, mypy, pre-commit
- `benchmark`: scikit-learn, lmfit, pandas
- `notebook`: jupyter, matplotlib

### 6. Summary: Existing vs. Needs Building

| **Parallel Workers** | **NOT PORTED** | `pypge/pypge/parallel.py` |

The evaluation back-end (model, optimize, metrics, evaluate) is complete and well-tested. The PGE search loop -- expression expansion, selection, prioritization, memoization, and the main search orchestration -- remains to be built on top of this foundation.

42:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,
43:     *x_inputs: jnp.ndarray,
44:     max_iter: int = 200,
45:     method: str = "lm",
46: ) -> FitResult:
47:     """Fit the coefficients of *model* to minimise prediction error.

49:     Parameters
50:     ----------
51:     model:
52:         A :class:`JAXModel` whose ``jax_fun`` will be used.
53:     y_true:
54:         Target values, shape ``(n_samples,)``.
55:     *x_inputs:
56:         Input-variable arrays, each shape ``(n_samples,)``.
57:     max_iter:
58:         Maximum optimisation iterations.
59:     method:
60:         Optimiser to use: ``"lm"`` (Levenberg-Marquardt, default) or
61:         ``"ls"`` (``jax.scipy.optimize.least_squares``).
62: 
63:     Returns
64:     -------
65:     FitResult
66:     """
67:     y_true = jnp.asarray(y_true, dtype=jnp.float64)
68: 
69:     # Build a zero-arg predict that captures x_inputs
70:     def predict(coefs: jnp.ndarray) -> jnp.ndarray:
71:         return model.jax_fun(coefs, *x_inputs)
72: 
73:     # Initialize coefficients to zeros with the right size
74:     x0 = jnp.zeros(model.n_coeffs, dtype=jnp.float64)
75: 
76:     if method == "lm":
77:         return fit_levenberg_marquardt(predict, y_true, x0=x0, max_iter=max_iter)
78:     elif method == "ls":
79:         from pge_jax.optimize import fit_least_squares
80: 
81:         return fit_least_squares(predict, y_true, x0=x0, max_iter=max_iter)
82:     else:
83:         raise ValueError(f"Unknown method: {method!r}")
84: 
85: 
86: def predict(
87:     model: JAXModel,
88:     coefs: jnp.ndarray,
89:     *x_inputs: jnp.ndarray,
90: ) -> jnp.ndarray:
91:     """Evaluate the fitted model at the given inputs."""
92:     return model.jax_fun(jnp.asarray(coefs, dtype=jnp.float64), *x_inputs)
93:

97:     y_true: jnp.ndarray,

99:     n_params: int | None = None,
100: ) -> EvalResult:
101:     """Compute all standard regression metrics.
102: 
103:     Parameters
104:     ----------
105:     y_true:

112:     """

Now I have a thorough understanding of both repos. Let me plan the port of the PGE search loop. I need to create several new modules in `pge_jax/`:

Let me trace through the logic more carefully—when I call lambdify with all symbols, it creates a function with one argument per symbol in sorted order, so I need to make sure the wrapper correctly unpacks and passes these arguments. I see the issue now—when there are no coefficients, `args` becomes empty, but `jax_fun` still expects variable arguments. The `*args` unpacking should handle this correctly, passing the variables as positional arguments. Let me trace through the actual flow: `self.jax_fun` is called with the coefficient array and variables, then unpacked into `*args` inside the lambda, and finally passed to `jax_fun` which receives them as separate positional arguments.

But there's a problem when there are no coefficients at all—the original symbols list is just the variables, and the lambda tries to unpack an empty coefficient array and pass the variables, which might not align with what `jax_fun` expects.

Actually, thinking through this more carefully: if `coeffs` is empty and `vars` has symbols like `[x, y]`, then `args` becomes `[x_arr, y_arr]`, `arg_names` is `['x', 'y']`, and `jax_fun` gets called with those two arrays as positional arguments. Since `jax_fun` was lambdified with just those same symbols, it should work fine.

For the case where there are no variables either, `args` would be empty and `jax_fun` would be called with no arguments, which should also be fine since it was lambdified with no symbols.

So the existing `jax_fun` logic handles all these edge cases correctly. Now I need to think about where the Jacobian computation fits in—currently it's using `jax.jacfwd` over all coefficients, but I should reconsider whether that's the right approach.

The Jacobian should only be computed with respect to coefficients, not input variables, since those are the parameters being optimized. 1: from sympy import preorder_traversal, numbers, Symbol

4: C = Symbol("C")
5: ## Filters on expressions
6: #
7: #  Each filter should take both a model and expression
8: #  So that the API is uniform, but we can access both
9: #  the model attributes and the (sub)expressions recursively
10: 
11: 
12: def filter_models(models, filters):
13: 	ret = []
14: 	for modl in models:
15: 		if not filter_model(modl, modl.orig, filters):
16: 			ret.append(modl)
17: 	return ret
18: 
19: def filter_model(modl, expr, filters):
20: 	for e in preorder_traversal(expr):
21: 		for f in filters:
22: 			if f(modl, e):
23: 				return True
24: 	return False
25: 
26: 
27: def filter_just_C(modl,expr):
28: 	if modl.orig is C or modl.orig == C or modl.orig.is_Number:
29: 		return True
30: 	return False
31: 
32: def filter_no_C(modl,expr):
33: 	if len(modl.cs) == 0:
34: 		return True
35: 	return False
36: 
37: def filter_too_big(modl, expr, big=64):
38: 	if modl.size() > big:
39: 		return True
40: 	return False
41: 
42: def filter_has_int_coeff(modl, expr):
43: 	if expr.is_Mul:
44: 			cs, _ = expr.as_coeff_Mul()
45: 			if type(cs) != numbers.One:
46: 				return True
47: 	if expr.is_Add:
48: 		cs, _ = expr.as_coeff_Add()
49: 		if type(cs) != numbers.Zero:
50: 			return True
51: 	return False
52: 
53: def filter_has_big_pow(modl, expr, big=6):
54: 	if expr.is_Pow:
55: 		B,E = expr.as_base_exp()
56: 		if abs(E) > big:
57: 			return True
58: 	return False
59: 
60: def filter_has_coeff_pow(modl, expr):
61: 	if expr.is_Pow:
62: 		B,E = expr.as_base_exp()
63: 		if B is C or B == C or B.is_Number:
64: 			return True
65: 	return False
66: 
67:

15: 		norm = True

40: 			vals.append(vs)

72: 			rp = p.index(")")
73: 			W = float(p[lp+1:rp])
74: 		if p[0] == "-":

76: 		elif p[0] == "+":
77: 			weights.append(1.0 * W)
78: 		else:
79: 			print("UNSIGNED FITNESS PARAMETER!!!")
80: 	print("weights: ", weights)
81: 	return tuple(weights)

**Output:**

<path>/Users/tony/verdverm/pge-jax/pypge/pypge/selection.py</path>
<type>file</type>
<content>
1: """
2: Taken from https://github.com/DEAP/deap
3: 
4: cause we want to fix the random aspect
5: SPEA-II is where it is
6: """
7: 
8: from __future__ import division
9: import bisect
10: import math
11: import random
12: random.seed(23)
13: 
14: from itertools import chain
15: from operator import attrgetter, itemgetter
16: from collections import defaultdict
17: 
18: ######################################
19: # Non-Dominated Sorting   (NSGA-II)  #
20: ######################################
21: 
22: def selNSGA2(individuals, k, nd='standard'):
23:     """Apply NSGA-II selection operator on the *individuals*. Usually, the
24:     size of *individuals* will be larger than *k* because any individual
25:     present in *individuals* will appear in the returned list at most once.
26:     Having the size of *individuals* equals to *k* will have no effect other
27:     than sorting the population according to their front rank. The
28:     list returned contains references to the input *individuals*. For more
29:     details on the NSGA-II operator see [Deb2002]_.
30:     
31:     :param individuals: A list of individuals to select from.
32:     :param k: The number of individuals to select.
33:     :param nd: Specify the non-dominated algorithm to use: 'standard' or 'log'.
34:     :returns: A list of selected individuals.
35:     
36:     .. [Deb2002] Deb, Pratab, Agarwal, and Meyarivan, "A fast elitist
37:        non-dominated sorting genetic algorithm for multi-objective
38:        optimization: NSGA-II", 2002.
39:     """
40:     if nd == 'standard':
41:         pareto_fronts = sortNondominated(individuals, k)
42:     elif nd == 'log':
43:         pareto_fronts = sortLogNondominated(individuals, k)
44:     else:
45:         raise Exception('selNSGA2: The choice of non-dominated sorting '
46:                         'method "{0}" is invalid.'.format(nd))
47: 
48:     for front in pareto_fronts:
49:         assignCrowdingDist(front)
50:     
51:     chosen = list(chain(*pareto_fronts[:-1]))
52:     k = k - len(chosen)
53:     if k > 0:
54:         sorted_front = sorted(pareto_fronts[-1], key=attrgetter("fitness.crowding_dist"), reverse=True)
55:         chosen.extend(sorted_front[:k])
56:         
57:     return chosen
58: 
59: def sortNondominated(individuals, k, first_front_only=False):
60:     """Sort the first *k* *individuals* into different nondomination levels 
61:     using the "Fast Nondominated Sorting Approach" proposed by Deb et al.,
62:     see [Deb2002]_. This algorithm has a time complexity of :math:`O(MN^2)`, 
63:     where :math:`M` is the number of objectives and :math:`N` the number of 
64:     individuals.
65:     
66:     :param individuals: A list of individuals to select from.
67:     :param k: The number of individuals to select.
68:     :param first_front_only: If :obj:`True` sort only the first front and
69:                              exit.
70:     :returns: A list of Pareto fronts (lists), the first list includes 
71:               nondominated individuals.
72: 
73:     .. [Deb2002] Deb, Pratab, Agarwal, and Meyarivan, "A fast elitist
74:        non-dominated sorting genetic algorithm for multi-objective
75:        optimization: NSGA-II", 2002.
76:     """
77:     if k == 0:
78:         return []
79: 
80:     map_fit_ind = defaultdict(list)
81:     for ind in individuals:
82:         map_fit_ind[ind.fitness].append(ind)
83:     fits = list(map_fit_ind.keys())
84:     
85:     current_front = []
86:     next_front = []
87:     dominating_fits = defaultdict(int)
88:     dominated_fits = defaultdict(list)
89:     
90:     # Rank first Pareto front
91:     for i, fit_i in enumerate(fits):
92:         for fit_j in fits[i+1:]:
93:             if fit_i.dominates(fit_j):
94:                 dominating_fits[fit_j] += 1
95:                 dominated_fits[fit_i].append(fit_j)
96:             elif fit_j.dominates(fit_i):
97:                 dominating_fits[fit_i] += 1
98:                 dominated_fits[fit_j].append(fit_i)
99:         if dominating_fits[fit_i] == 0:
100:             current_front.append(fit_i)
101:     
102:     fronts = [[]]
103:     for fit in current_front:
104:         fronts[-1].extend(map_fit_ind[fit])
105:     pareto_sorted = len(fronts[-1])
106: 
107:     # Rank the next front until all individuals are sorted or 
108:     # the given number of individual are sorted.
109:     if not first_front_only:
110:         N = min(len(individuals), k)
111:         while pareto_sorted < N:
112:             fronts.append([])
113:             for fit_p in current_front:
114:                 for fit_d in dominated_fits[fit_p]:
115:                     dominating_fits[fit_d] -= 1
116:                     if dominating_fits[fit_d] == 0:
117:                         next_front.append(fit_d)
118:                         pareto_sorted += len(map_fit_ind[fit_d])
119:                         fronts[-1].extend(map_fit_ind[fit_d])
120:             current_front = next_front
121:             next_front = []
122:     
123:     return fronts
124: 
125: def assignCrowdingDist(individuals):
126:     """Assign a crowding distance to each individual's fitness. The 
127:     crowding distance can be retrieve via the :attr:`crowding_dist` 
128:     attribute of each individual's fitness.
129:     """
130:     if len(individuals) == 0:
131:         return
132:     
133:     distances = [0.0] * len(individuals)
134:     crowd = [(ind.fitness.values, i) for i, ind in enumerate(individuals)]
135:     
136:     nobj = len(individuals[0].fitness.values)
137:     
138:     for i in range(nobj):
139:         crowd.sort(key=lambda element: element[0][i])
140:         distances[crowd[0][1]] = float("inf")
141:         distances[crowd[-1][1]] = float("inf")
142:         if crowd[-1][0][i] == crowd[0][0][i]:
143:             continue
144:         norm = nobj * float(crowd[-1][0][i] - crowd[0][0][i])
145:         for prev, cur, next in zip(crowd[:-2], crowd[1:-1], crowd[2:]):
146:             distances[cur[1]] += (next[0][i] - prev[0][i]) / norm
147: 
148:     for i, dist in enumerate(distances):
149:         individuals[i].fitness.crowding_dist = dist
150: 
151: def selTournamentDCD(individuals, k):
152:     """Tournament selection based on dominance (D) between two individuals, if
153:     the two individuals do not interdominate the selection is made
154:     based on crowding distance (CD). The *individuals* sequence length has to
155:     be a multiple of 4. Starting from the beginning of the selected
156:     individuals, two consecutive individuals will be different (assuming all
157:     individuals in the input list are unique). Each individual from the input
158:     list won't be selected more than twice.
159:     
160:     This selection requires the individuals to have a :attr:`crowding_dist`
161:     attribute, which can be set by the :func:`assignCrowdingDist` function.
162:     
163:     :param individuals: A list of individuals to select from.
164:     :param k: The number of individuals to select.
165:     :returns: A list of selected individuals.
166:     """
167:     def tourn(ind1, ind2):
168:         if ind1.fitness.dominates(ind2.fitness):
169:             return ind1
170:         elif ind2.fitness.dominates(ind1.fitness):
171:             return ind2
172: 
173:         if ind1.fitness.crowding_dist < ind2.fitness.crowding_dist:
174:             return ind2
175:         elif ind1.fitness.crowding_dist > ind2.fitness.crowding_dist:
176:             return ind1
177: 
178:         if random.random() <= 0.5:
179:             return ind1
180:         return ind2
181: 
182:     individuals_1 = random.sample(individuals, len(individuals))
183:     individuals_2 = random.sample(individuals, len(individuals))
184: 
185:     chosen = []
186:     for i in range(0, k, 4):
187:         chosen.append(tourn(individuals_1[i],   individuals_1[i+1]))
188:         chosen.append(tourn(individuals_1[i+2], individuals_1[i+3]))
189:         chosen.append(tourn(individuals_2[i],   individuals_2[i+1]))
190:         chosen.append(tourn(individuals_2[i+2], individuals_2[i+3]))
191: 
192:     return chosen
193: 
194: #######################################
195: # Generalized Reduced runtime ND sort #
196: #######################################
197: 
198: def identity(obj):
199:     """Returns directly the argument *obj*.
200:     """
201:     return obj
202: 
203: def isDominated(wvalues1, wvalues2):
204:     """Returns whether or not *wvalues1* dominates *wvalues2*.
205:     
206:     :param wvalues1: The weighted fitness values that would be dominated.
207:     :param wvalues2: The weighted fitness values of the dominant.
208:     :returns: :obj:`True` if wvalues2 dominates wvalues1, :obj:`False`
209:               otherwise.
210:     """
211:     not_equal = False
212:     for self_wvalue, other_wvalue in zip(wvalues1, wvalues2):
213:         if self_wvalue > other_wvalue:
214:             return False
215:         elif self_wvalue < other_wvalue:
216:             not_equal = True
217:     return not_equal
218: 
219: def median(seq, key=identity):
220:     """Returns the median of *seq* - the numeric value separating the higher 
221:     half of a sample from the lower half. If there is an even number of 
222:     elements in *seq*, it returns the mean of the two middle values.
223:     """
224:     sseq = sorted(seq, key=key)
225:     length = len(seq)
226:     if length % 2 == 1:
227:         return key(sseq[(length - 1) // 2])
228:     else:
229:         return (key(sseq[(length - 1) // 2]) + key(sseq[length // 2])) / 2.0
230: 
231: def sortLogNondominated(individuals, k, first_front_only=False):
232:     """Sort *individuals* in pareto non-dominated fronts using the Generalized
233:     Reduced Run-Time Complexity Non-Dominated Sorting Algorithm presented by
234:     Fortin et al. (2013).
235:     
236:     :param individuals: A list of individuals to select from.
237:     :returns: A list of Pareto fronts (lists), with the first list being the
238:               true Pareto front.
239:     """
240:     if k == 0:
241:         return []
242:     
243:     #Separate individuals according to unique fitnesses
244:     unique_fits = defaultdict(list)
245:     for i, ind in enumerate(individuals):
246:         unique_fits[ind.fitness.wvalues].append(ind)
247:     
248:     #Launch the sorting algorithm
249:     obj = len(individuals[0].fitness.wvalues)-1
250:     fitnesses = list(unique_fits.keys())
251:     front = dict.fromkeys(fitnesses, 0)
252: 
253:     # Sort the fitnesses lexicographically.
254:     fitnesses.sort(reverse=True)
255:     sortNDHelperA(fitnesses, obj, front)    
256:     
257:     #Extract individuals from front list here
258:     nbfronts = max(front.values())+1
259:     pareto_fronts = [[] for i in range(nbfronts)]
260:     for fit in fitnesses:
261:         index = front[fit]
262:         pareto_fronts[index].extend(unique_fits[fit])
263: 
264:     # Keep only the fronts required to have k individuals.
265:     if not first_front_only:
266:         count = 0
267:         for i, front in enumerate(pareto_fronts):
268:             count += len(front)
269:             if count >= k:
270:                 return pareto_fronts[:i+1]
271:         return pareto_fronts
272:     else:
273:         return pareto_fronts[0]
274: 
275: def sortNDHelperA(fitnesses, obj, front):
276:     """Create a non-dominated sorting of S on the first M objectives"""
277:     if len(fitnesses) < 2:
278:         return
279:     elif len(fitnesses) == 2:
280:         # Only two individuals, compare them and adjust front number
281:         s1, s2 = fitnesses[0], fitnesses[1]
282:         if isDominated(s2[:obj+1], s1[:obj+1]):
283:             front[s2] = max(front[s2], front[s1] + 1)
284:     elif obj == 1:
285:         sweepA(fitnesses, front)
286:     elif len(frozenset(map(itemgetter(obj), fitnesses))) == 1:
287:         #All individuals for objective M are equal: go to objective M-1
288:         sortNDHelperA(fitnesses, obj-1, front)
289:     else:
290:         # More than two individuals, split list and then apply recursion
291:         best, worst = splitA(fitnesses, obj)
292:         sortNDHelperA(best, obj, front)
293:         sortNDHelperB(best, worst, obj-1, front)
294:         sortNDHelperA(worst, obj, front)
295: 
296: def splitA(fitnesses, obj):
297:     """Partition the set of fitnesses in two according to the median of
298:     the objective index *obj*. The values equal to the median are put in
299:     the set containing the least elements.
300:     """
301:     median_ = median(fitnesses, itemgetter(obj))
302:     best_a, worst_a = [], []
303:     best_b, worst_b = [], []
304: 
305:     for fit in fitnesses:
306:         if fit[obj] > median_:
307:             best_a.append(fit)
308:             best_b.append(fit)
309:         elif fit[obj] < median_:
310:             worst_a.append(fit)
311:             worst_b.append(fit)
312:         else:
313:             best_a.append(fit)
314:             worst_b.append(fit)
315: 
316:     balance_a = abs(len(best_a) - len(worst_a))
317:     balance_b = abs(len(best_b) - len(worst_b))
318: 
319:     if balance_a <= balance_b:
320:         return best_a, worst_a
321:     else:
322:         return best_b, worst_b
323: 
324: def sweepA(fitnesses, front):
325:     """Update rank number associated to the fitnesses according
326:     to the first two objectives using a geometric sweep procedure.
327:     """
328:     stairs = [-fitnesses[0][1]]
329:     fstairs = [fitnesses[0]]  
330:     for fit in fitnesses[1:]:
331:         idx = bisect.bisect_right(stairs, -fit[1])
332:         if 0 < idx <= len(stairs):
333:             fstair = max(fstairs[:idx], key=front.__getitem__)
334:             front[fit] = max(front[fit], front[fstair]+1)
335:         for i, fstair in enumerate(fstairs[idx:], idx):
336:             if front[fstair] == front[fit]:
337:                 del stairs[i]
338:                 del fstairs[i]
339:                 break
340:         stairs.insert(idx, -fit[1])
341:         fstairs.insert(idx, fit)
342: 
343: def sortNDHelperB(best, worst, obj, front):
344:     """Assign front numbers to the solutions in H according to the solutions 
345:     in L. The solutions in L are assumed to have correct front numbers and the 
346:     solutions in H are not compared with each other, as this is supposed to 
347:     happen after sortNDHelperB is called."""
348:     key = itemgetter(obj)    
349:     if len(worst) == 0 or len(best) == 0:
350:         #One of the lists is empty: nothing to do
351:         return
352:     elif len(best) == 1 or len(worst) == 1:
353:         #One of the lists has one individual: compare directly
354:         for hi in worst:
355:             for li in best:
356:                 if isDominated(hi[:obj+1], li[:obj+1]) or hi[:obj+1] == li[:obj+1]:
357:                     front[hi] = max(front[hi], front[li] + 1)
358:     elif obj == 1:
359:         sweepB(best, worst, front)
360:     elif key(min(best, key=key)) >= key(max(worst, key=key)):
361:         #All individuals from L dominate H for objective M:
362:         #Also supports the case where every individuals in L and H 
363:         #has the same value for the current objective
364:         #Skip to objective M-1
365:         sortNDHelperB(best, worst, obj-1, front)
366:     elif key(max(best, key=key)) >= key(min(worst, key=key)):
367:         best1, best2, worst1, worst2 = splitB(best, worst, obj)
368:         sortNDHelperB(best1, worst1, obj, front)
369:         sortNDHelperB(best1, worst2, obj-1, front)
370:         sortNDHelperB(best2, worst2, obj, front)
371: 
372: def splitB(best, worst, obj):
373:     """Split both best individual and worst sets of fitnesses according
374:     to the median of objective *obj* computed on the set containing the
375:     most elements. The values equal to the median are attributed so as 
376:     to balance the four resulting sets as much as possible.
377:     """
378:     median_ = median(best if len(best) > len(worst) else worst, itemgetter(obj))
379:     best1_a, best2_a, best1_b, best2_b = [], [], [], []
380:     for fit in best:
381:         if fit[obj] > median_:
382:             best1_a.append(fit)
383:             best1_b.append(fit)
384:         elif fit[obj] < median_:
385:             best2_a.append(fit)
386:             best2_b.append(fit)
387:         else:
388:             best1_a.append(fit)
389:             best2_b.append(fit)
390:     
391:     worst1_a, worst2_a, worst1_b, worst2_b = [], [], [], []        
392:     for fit in worst:
393:         if fit[obj] > median_:
394:             worst1_a.append(fit)
395:             worst1_b.append(fit)
396:         elif fit[obj] < median_:
397:             worst2_a.append(fit)
398:             worst2_b.append(fit)
399:         else:
400:             worst1_a.append(fit)
401:             worst2_b.append(fit)
402:     
403:     balance_a = abs(len(best1_a) - len(best2_a) + len(worst1_a) - len(worst2_a))
404:     balance_b = abs(len(best1_b) - len(best2_b) + len(worst1_b) - len(worst2_b))
405: 
406:     if balance_a <= balance_b:
407:         return best1_a, best2_a, worst1_a, worst2_a
408:     else:
409:         return best1_b, best2_b, worst1_b, worst2_b
410: 
411: def sweepB(best, worst, front):
412:     """Adjust the rank number of the worst fitnesses according to
413:     the best fitnesses on the first two objectives using a sweep
414:     procedure.
415:     """
416:     stairs, fstairs = [], []
417:     iter_best = iter(best)
418:     next_best = next(iter_best, False)
419:     for h in worst:
420:         while next_best and h[:2] <= next_best[:2]:
421:             insert = True
422:             for i, fstair in enumerate(fstairs):
423:                 if front[fstair] == front[next_best]:
424:                     if fstair[1] > next_best[1]:
425:                         insert = False
426:                     else:
427:                         del stairs[i], fstairs[i]
428:                     break
429:             if insert:
430:                 idx = bisect.bisect_right(stairs, -next_best[1])
431:                 stairs.insert(idx, -next_best[1])
432:                 fstairs.insert(idx, next_best)
433:             next_best = next(iter_best, False)
434: 
435:         idx = bisect.bisect_right(stairs, -h[1])
436:         if 0 < idx <= len(stairs):
437:             fstair = max(fstairs[:idx], key=front.__getitem__)
438:             front[h] = max(front[h], front[fstair]+1)
439: 
440: ######################################
441: # Strength Pareto         (SPEA-II)  #
442: ######################################
443: 
444: def selSPEA2(individuals, k):
445:     """Apply SPEA-II selection operator on the *individuals*. Usually, the
446:     size of *individuals* will be larger than *n* because any individual
447:     present in *individuals* will appear in the returned list at most once.
448:     Having the size of *individuals* equals to *n* will have no effect other
449:     than sorting the population according to a strength Pareto scheme. The
450:     list returned contains references to the input *individuals*. For more
451:     details on the SPEA-II operator see [Zitzler2001]_.
452:     
453:     :param individuals: A list of individuals to select from.
454:     :param k: The number of individuals to select.
455:     :returns: A list of selected individuals.
456:     
457:     .. [Zitzler2001] Zitzler, Laumanns and Thiele, "SPEA 2: Improving the
458:        strength Pareto evolutionary algorithm", 2001.
459:     """
460:     N = len(individuals)
461:     L = len(individuals[0].fitness.values)
462:     K = math.sqrt(N)
463:     strength_fits = [0] * N
464:     fits = [0] * N
465:     dominating_inds = [list() for i in range(N)]
466:     
467:     for i, ind_i in enumerate(individuals):
468:         for j, ind_j in enumerate(individuals[i+1:], i+1):
469:             if ind_i.fitness.dominates(ind_j.fitness):
470:                 strength_fits[i] += 1
471:                 dominating_inds[j].append(i)
472:             elif ind_j.fitness.dominates(ind_i.fitness):
473:                 strength_fits[j] += 1
474:                 dominating_inds[i].append(j)
475:     
476:     for i in range(N):
477:         for j in dominating_inds[i]:
478:             fits[i] += strength_fits[j]
479:     
480:     # Choose all non-dominated individuals
481:     chosen_indices = [i for i in range(N) if fits[i] < 1]
482:     
483:     if len(chosen_indices) < k:     # The archive is too small
484:         for i in range(N):
485:             distances = [0.0] * N
486:             for j in range(i + 1, N):
487:                 dist = 0.0
488:                 for l in range(L):
489:                     val = individuals[i].fitness.values[l] - \
490:                           individuals[j].fitness.values[l]
491:                     dist += val * val
492:                 distances[j] = dist
493:             kth_dist = _randomizedSelect(distances, 0, N - 1, K)
494:             density = 1.0 / (kth_dist + 2.0)
495:             fits[i] += density
496:             
497:         next_indices = [(fits[i], i) for i in range(N)
498:                         if not i in chosen_indices]
499:         next_indices.sort()
500:         chosen_indices += [i for _, i in next_indices[:k - len(chosen_indices)]]
501:                 
502:     elif len(chosen_indices) > k:   # The archive is too large
503:         N = len(chosen_indices)
504:         distances = [[0.0] * N for i in range(N)]
505:         sorted_indices = [[0] * N for i in range(N)]
506:         for i in range(N):
507:             for j in range(i + 1, N):
508:                 dist = 0.0
509:                 for l in range(L):
510:                     val = individuals[chosen_indices[i]].fitness.values[l] - \
511:                           individuals[chosen_indices[j]].fitness.values[l]
512:                     dist += val * val
513:                 distances[i][j] = dist
514:                 distances[j][i] = dist
515:             distances[i][i] = -1
516:         
517:         # Insert sort is faster than quick sort for short arrays
518:         for i in range(N):
519:             for j in range(1, N):
520:                 l = j
521:                 while l > 0 and distances[i][j] < distances[i][sorted_indices[i][l - 1]]:
522:                     sorted_indices[i][l] = sorted_indices[i][l - 1]
523:                     l -= 1
524:                 sorted_indices[i][l] = j
525:         
526:         size = N
527:         to_remove = []
528:         while size > k:
529:             # Search for minimal distance
530:             min_pos = 0
531:             for i in range(1, N):
532:                 for j in range(1, size):
533:                     dist_i_sorted_j = distances[i][sorted_indices[i][j]]
534:                     dist_min_sorted_j = distances[min_pos][sorted_indices[min_pos][j]]
535:                     
536:                     if dist_i_sorted_j < dist_min_sorted_j:
537:                         min_pos = i
538:                         break
539:                     elif dist_i_sorted_j > dist_min_sorted_j:
540:                         break
541:             
542:             # Remove minimal distance from sorted_indices
543:             for i in range(N):
544:                 distances[i][min_pos] = float("inf")
545:                 distances[min_pos][i] = float("inf")
546:                 
547:                 for j in range(1, size - 1):
548:                     if sorted_indices[i][j] == min_pos:
549:                         sorted_indices[i][j] = sorted_indices[i][j + 1]
550:                         sorted_indices[i][j + 1] = min_pos
551:             
552:             # Remove corresponding individual from chosen_indices
553:             to_remove.append(min_pos)
554:             size -= 1
555:         
556:         for index in reversed(sorted(to_remove)):
557:             del chosen_indices[index]
558:     
559:     return [individuals[i] for i in chosen_indices]
560:     
561: def _randomizedSelect(array, begin, end, i):
562:     """Allows to select the ith smallest element from array without sorting it.
563:     Runtime is expected to be O(n).
564:     """
565:     if begin == end:
566:         return array[begin]
567:     q = _randomizedPartition(array, begin, end)
568:     k = q - begin + 1
569:     if i < k:
570:         return _randomizedSelect(array, begin, q, i)
571:     else:
572:         return _randomizedSelect(array, q + 1, end, i - k)
573: 
574: def _medianIndexThree(array, i1, i2, i3):
575:     c = cmp(array[i1], array[i2])
576:     if c < 0:
577:         c2 = cmp(array[i1],array[i3])
578:         return i1 if c2 < 0 else i2
579:     else:
580:         c2 = cmp(array[i2],array[i3])
581:         return i2 if c2 < 0 else i3
582: 
583: def _randomizedPartition(array, begin, end):
584:     # borrowed from [ https://golang.org/src/sort/sort.go :: doPivot]
585:     # finds the median value of 3 or 9 elements, depending on the length
586:     m = begin + (end-begin)//2 # Written like this to avoid integer overflow.
587:     b,e = begin, end
588:     if end-begin > 40:
589:         # Tukey's ``Ninther,'' median of three medians of three.
590:         s = (end - begin) // 8
591:         b = _medianIndexThree(array, begin, begin+s, begin+2*s)
592:         m = _medianIndexThree(array, m, m-s, m+s)
593:         e = _medianIndexThree(array, end-1, end-1-s, end-1-2*s)
594:     m = _medianIndexThree(array, b, m, e-1)
595: 
596:     array[begin], array[m] = array[m], array[begin]
597:     return _partition(array, begin, end)
598:     
599: def _partition(array, begin, end):
600:     x = array[begin]
601:     i = begin - 1
602:     j = end + 1
603:     while True:
604:         j -= 1
605:         while array[j] > x:
606:             j -= 1
607:         i += 1
608:         while array[i] < x:
609:             i += 1
610:         if i < j:
611:             array[i], array[j] = array[j], array[i]
612:         else:
613:             return j
614: 
615: 
616: __all__ = ['selNSGA2', 'selSPEA2', 'sortNondominated', 'sortLogNondominated',
617:            'selTournamentDCD']

(End of file - total 617 lines)
</content>

127: 		# print("with_c_xs4_muls", self.with_c_xs4_muls)
128: 		
129: 		self.wout_c_linear_funcs = []
130: 		self.wout_c_nonlin_funcs = []
131: 		self.with_c_linear_funcs = []
132: 		self.with_c_nonlin_funcs = []
133: 		if funcs is not None:
134: 			self.wout_c_linear_funcs = [ f(x) for f in funcs for x in self.wout_c_xs1_muls]
135: 			self.wout_c_nonlin_funcs = [ f(C*x+C) for f in funcs for x in self.wout_c_xs1_muls]
136: 			self.with_c_linear_funcs = [ C*f(x) for f in funcs for x in self.wout_c_xs1_muls]
137: 			self.with_c_nonlin_funcs = [ C*f(C*x+C) for f in funcs for x in self.wout_c_xs1_muls]
138: 
139: 		# print("wout_c_linear_funcs", self.wout_c_linear_funcs)
140: 		# print("wout_c_nonlin_funcs", self.wout_c_nonlin_funcs)
141: 		# print("with_c_linear_funcs", self.with_c_linear_funcs)
142: 		# print("with_c_nonlin_funcs", self.with_c_nonlin_funcs)
143:

145: 		self.wout_c_func_exprs = []
146: 		if self.func_level == "linear":
147: 			self.with_c_func_exprs = self.with_c_linear_funcs + [ f**(-1) for f in self.with_c_linear_funcs ]
148: 			self.wout_c_func_exprs = self.wout_c_linear_funcs + [ f**(-1) for f in self.wout_c_linear_funcs ]
149: 		elif self.func_level in ["nonlin", "nonlinear"]:
150: 			self.with_c_func_exprs = self.with_c_nonlin_funcs + [ f**(-1) for f in self.with_c_nonlin_funcs ]
151: 			self.wout_c_func_exprs = self.wout_c_nonlin_funcs + [ f**(-1) for f in self.wout_c_nonlin_funcs ]
152: 		else:
153: 			print("UNKNOWN FUNC_LEVEL!!")
154: 			return
155: 
156: 		self.init_var_subs()
157: 		self.init_add_extends()
158: 		self.init_mul_extends()
159: 
160: 	def first_exprs(self):
161: 		
162: 		mul_exprs = []
163: 		if self.init_level == "low":
164: 			if len(self.xs) > 3:
165: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs1_muls
166: 			else:
167: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs2_muls
168: 		elif self.init_level == "med":
169: 			if len(self.xs) > 3:
170: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs1_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
171: 			elif len(self.xs) > 1:
172: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs2_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
173: 			else:
174: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs3_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
175: 		elif self.init_level == "high":
176: 			if len(self.xs) > 3:
177: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs2_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
178: 			elif len(self.xs) > 1:
179: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs3_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
180: 			else:
181: 				mul_exprs = self.with_c_xs4_muls + self.with_c_func_exprs
182: 		else:
183: 			print("UNKNOWN INIT_LEVEL!!")
184: 			return
185: 
186: 		print("mul_exprs: ", len(mul_exprs), mul_exprs)
187: 
188: 		mid_exprs = mul_exprs
189: 		print("mid_exprs: ", len(mid_exprs))
190: 		add_exprs = [ tpl[0] + tpl[1] for tpl in combos_woutR(mid_exprs, 2)]
191: 		if self.init_level == "high":
192: 			add_exprs += [ tpl[0] + tpl[1] + tpl[2] for tpl in combos_woutR(mid_exprs, 3)]
193: 		print("add_exprs: ", len(add_exprs))
194: 
195: 		exprs_set = mid_exprs + add_exprs + self.with_c_func_exprs
196: 		print("exprs_set: ", len(exprs_set))
197: 
198: 		# always add the plus C
199: 		plus_C_exprs = [ sympy.Add( expr, C ) for expr in exprs_set]
200: 		ret_exprs = exprs_set + plus_C_exprs
201: 		print("ret_exprs", len(ret_exprs))
202: 
203: 		## UNIQUIFY THE RESULTS
204: 		ret_exprs = self._uniquify(ret_exprs)
205: 
206: 		models = [model.Model(e, xs=self.xs) for e in ret_exprs]
207: 		for m in models:
208: 			m.gen_relation = "first_gen"
209: 			m.parent_id = -1
210: 
211: 		return models

285: 	def grow(self, M):
286: 
287: 		var_expands = self._var_sub(M.orig)
288: 		add_expands = self._add_extend(M.orig)
289: 		mul_expands = self._mul_extend(M.orig)
290: 
291: 		var_expands_C = [ self._toggle_plus_C(e) for e in var_expands ]
292: 		add_expands_C = [ self._toggle_plus_C(e) for e in add_expands ]
293: 		mul_expands_C = [ self._toggle_plus_C(e) for e in mul_expands ]
294: 
295: 		var_expands = self._uniquify(var_expands + var_expands_C)
296: 		add_expands = self._uniquify(add_expands + add_expands_C)
297: 		mul_expands = self._uniquify(mul_expands + mul_expands_C)
298: 		
299: 		add_biggers = []
300: 		if self.add_xtop:
301: 			add_biggers = self._add_extend_top_level(M.orig)
302: 			add_biggers_C = [ self._toggle_plus_C(e) for e in add_biggers ]
303: 			add_biggers = self._uniquify(add_biggers + add_biggers_C)
304: 
305: 		shrunk = []
306: 		if self.shrinker:
307: 			shrunk = self._shrinker(M.orig)
308: 
309: 		var_models = [model.Model(e, p_id=M.id, reln="var_xpnd") for e in var_expands if e != C]
310: 		big_models = [model.Model(e, p_id=M.id, reln="add_bigr") for e in add_biggers if e != C]
311: 		add_models = [model.Model(e, p_id=M.id, reln="add_xpnd") for e in add_expands if e != C]
312: 		mul_models = [model.Model(e, p_id=M.id, reln="mul_xpnd") for e in mul_expands if e != C]
313: 		shrunk_models = [model.Model(e, p_id=M.id, reln="shrunk") for e in shrunk if e != C]
314: 
315: 		models = var_models + big_models + add_models + mul_models + shrunk_models
316: 		return models
317: 
318: 
319: 	def _var_sub(self, expr, limit_sub=False, depth=1):
320: 		new_exprs = []
321: 		# only worry about non-atoms, cause we have to replace args
322: 		if not expr.is_Atom:
323: 			# make a list of args to this non-atom
324: 			# each member of the list is the original expr's args with one substitution made
325: 			args_sets = []
326: 			for i,e in enumerate(expr.args):
327: 				# if the current arg is also a non-atom, then recursion!
328: 				if not e.is_Atom:
329: 					## check to see if we are in some function besides ADD or MUL
330: 					## if so, limit what we substitute
331: 					lim_sub = limit_sub or not (e.is_Add or e.is_Mul)
332: 					# for each expr returned, we need to clone the current args
333: 					# and make the substitution, sorta like flattening?
334: 					ee = self._var_sub(e, lim_sub, depth=depth+1)
335: 					if len(ee) > 0:
336: 						# We made a substitution(s) on a variable down this branch!!
337: 						print(len(expr.args))
338: 						args_map = set(expr.args)
339: 						for vs in ee:
340: 							if self.grow_filter == True and expr.is_Add and vs in args_map:
341: 								continue
342: 							# clone current args
343: 							cloned_args = list(expr.args)
344: 							# replace this term in each
345: 							cloned_args[i] = vs
346: 							# append to the args_sets
347: 							args_sets.append(cloned_args)
348: 
349: 				elif e in self.xs:
350: 					## Lets make a variable substitution !!
351: 					## First, whats the context? what are we going to substitute?
352: 					sub_terms = None
353: 					if depth >= self.limiting_depth:
354: 						sub_terms = self.var_sub_dep_terms
355: 					else:
356: 						sub_terms = self.var_sub_terms
357: 					if limit_sub:
358: 						if depth >= self.limiting_depth:
359: 							sub_terms = self.var_sub_dep_lim_terms
360: 						else:
361: 							sub_terms = self.var_sub_lim_terms
362: 
363: 					# loop over sub_terms, subing for and create new arg sets
364: 					for vs in sub_terms:
365: 						# if self.grow_filter == True and expr.is_Add and vs in expr.args:
366: 						# 	continue
367: 						# clone current args
368: 						cloned_args = list(expr.args)
369: 						# replace this term in each
370: 						cloned_args[i] = vs
371: 						# append to the args_sets
372: 						args_sets.append(cloned_args)
373: 				else:
374: 					# we don't have to do anything, probably?
375: 					# coefficients?
376: 					pass
377: 
378: 			# finally, create all of the clones at the current level of recursion
379: 			for args in args_sets:
380: 				args = tuple(args)
381: 				tmp = expr.func(*args)
382: 				new_exprs.append(tmp)
383: 
384: 		ret_exprs = self._uniquify(new_exprs)
385: 		return ret_exprs
386: 
387: 	
388: 
389: 	def _add_extend_top_level(self, expr):
390: 		"""
391: 		this only extends a top-level addition, but in a more complex way with _mul_extend. NO recursion!
392: 		For each term in the addition, we do all possible mul_expands, and then append to the full Add.
393: 		This will likely create lots of duplicate, need to check on simplification, or at least grouping terms
394: 		"""
395: 		if expr.is_Add:
396: 			new_terms = []
397: 
398: 			for e in expr.args:
399: 				if e.is_Mul:
400: 					for term in self.mul_extend_terms:
401: 						cloned_args = list(e.args)
402: 						cloned_args.append(term)
403: 						new_mul = e.func(*cloned_args)
404: 						new_terms.append(new_mul)
405: 
406: 			new_exprs = []
407: 			print(len(expr.args))
408: 			args_map = set(expr.args)
409: 			for term in new_terms:
410: 				if self.grow_filter == True and term in args_map:
411: 					continue
412: 				cloned_args = list(expr.args)
413: 				cloned_args.append(term)
414: 				bigger_add = expr.func(*cloned_args)
415: 				new_exprs.append(bigger_add)
416: 
417: 			ret_exprs = self._uniquify(new_exprs)
418: 			return ret_exprs
419: 
420: 		else:
421: 			return []
